# Investigation: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update in Istio

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8c9b973 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/istio--f8c9b973 (mirror of istio/istio)
**Task Type:** Deep Causal Chain (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

An Istio service mesh operator reports that updating a DestinationRule in their cluster **silently fails to propagate** to Envoy sidecars. Specifically, when they have multiple DestinationRules for the same host (e.g., one defining subsets, another defining traffic policy), updating one of them does not trigger an xDS push — the Envoy sidecar continues serving the **stale** cluster and route configuration.

The operator has two DestinationRules for `reviews.default.svc.cluster.local`:

**DR-1 (traffic policy):**
```yaml
apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3
kind: DestinationRule
metadata:
  name: reviews-traffic-policy
  namespace: default
spec:
  host: reviews.default.svc.cluster.local
  trafficPolicy:
    connectionPool:
      tcp:
        maxConnections: 100
      http:
        h2UpgradePolicy: UPGRADE
```

**DR-2 (subsets):**
```yaml
apiVersion: networking.istio.io/v1alpha3
kind: DestinationRule
metadata:
  name: reviews-subsets
  namespace: default
spec:
  host: reviews.default.svc.cluster.local
  subsets:
    - name: v1
      labels:
        version: v1
    - name: v2
      labels:
        version: v2
```

When the operator updates `reviews-subsets` (e.g., adding a `v3` subset), the Envoy sidecar does **not** receive updated CDS/RDS config. Only restarting the pod picks up the change. Updating `reviews-traffic-policy` also has no effect.

Istio debug endpoint `GET /debug/config_dump` on the sidecar shows the old configuration even after the DestinationRule has been updated in the Kubernetes API server.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause of why updating a merged DestinationRule fails to trigger an xDS push, and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:

1. **How Istio merges multiple DestinationRules for the same host** — specifically the `mergeDestinationRule()` function in `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go` and how it combines subsets and traffic policies from multiple DRs into a single merged config
2. **How the merged DestinationRule loses identity metadata** — when two DRs are merged, only one DR's `config.Config` metadata (name/namespace) survives in the `consolidatedDestRules` structure. The metadata of contributing DRs is lost.
3. **How SidecarScope builds config dependencies** — the `AddConfigDependencies()` calls in `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` that register which config resources a proxy depends on. Specifically, how `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()` iterate over `destinationRules` and add `ConfigKey{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: dr.Name, Namespace: dr.Namespace}` for each DR
4. **The specific gap: only one DR's ConfigKey is registered** — because the merged DR has only one name/namespace, `AddConfigDependencies` registers only that one DR. The other contributing DR(s) are not tracked.
5. **How the xDS push filter uses DependsOnConfig** — when a config change event occurs, `pilot/pkg/xds/` calls `SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(configKey)` to decide if the proxy needs a push. If the updated DR is the one whose metadata was lost during merging, `DependsOnConfig` returns `false` and the push is **incorrectly skipped**.
6. **The relationship between PushContext.destinationRule() and the merge pipeline** — how `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` stores the `destinationRuleIndex` and how `destinationRule()` returns the merged config, obscuring the fact that multiple DRs contributed to it

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Causal Chain
<Ordered list: symptom → intermediate hops → root cause>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- The causal chain spans at least 4 packages: `pilot/pkg/model/`, `pilot/pkg/xds/`, `pilot/pkg/networking/core/`, and `pilot/pkg/config/`
- Focus on how the DestinationRule merging in `destination_rule.go` interacts with dependency tracking in `sidecar.go` and push filtering in the xDS layer

52-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. The report covers:

## Key Findings:

**Root Cause:** When multiple DestinationRules target the same host, only the **first DR's metadata** survives the merge in `consolidatedDestRules`. This causes only one DR's ConfigKey to be registered in the SidecarScope's `configDependencies` map. When the **other DR is updated**, its ConfigKey's hash is not found in the dependencies, so the xDS push is incorrectly filtered out and rejected.

**Affected Components:**
1. `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go` - Merges DRs but loses metadata identity
2. `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go` - Registers only one DR's ConfigKey in dependencies  
3. `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go` - Correctly filters based on dependencies but only has incomplete list
4. `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` - Stores merged DRs without tracking all contributors
5. `pilot/pkg/model/config.go` - Hash computation works correctly but only some keys are registered

**Causal Chain:** The failure flows from the xDS push filtering layer → dependency checking → incomplete registration → merging losing metadata. The last step in merging is where the first contributing DR's metadata is preserved while others are lost during the in-place merge into `consolidatedDestRules`.

The report includes specific file paths, line numbers, code evidence, diagnostic steps for verification, and three recommended fix strategies ranging from minimal necessary changes to more comprehensive approaches.

Note that it does not perform inheritance style merging.\n30: // IOW, given three dest rules (*.foo.com, *.foo.com, *.com), calling this function for\n31: // each config will result in a final dest rule set (*.foo.com, and *.com).\n32: //\n33: // The following is the merge logic:\n34: // 1. destRuleConfig.Meta)\n41: \tif mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {\n42: \t\t// `addRuleToProcessedDestRules` determines if the incoming destination rule would become a new unique entry in the processedDestRules list.\n43: \t\taddRuleToProcessedDestRules := true\n44: \t\tfor i, mdr := range mdrList {\n45: \t\t\texistingRule := mdr.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n46: \t\t\tif bothWithSelector && !selectorsMatch {\n51: \t\t\t\t// If the new destination rule and the existing one has workload selectors associated with them, skip merging\n52: \t\t\t\t// if the selectors do not match\n53: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n54: \t\t\t}\n55: \n56: \t\t\t// If both the destination rules are without a workload selector or with matching workload selectors, simply merge them.\n57: \t\t\t// If the incoming rule has a workload selector, it has to be merged with the existing rules with workload selector, and\n58: \t\t\t// at the same time added as a unique entry in the same host.\n74: \t\t\t// concatenate both of them -- essentially add subsets from one to other.\n75: \t\t\t// Note: we only add the subsets and do not overwrite anything else like exportTo or top is a wrapper over the Sidecar resource with some\n56: // preprocessed data to determine the list of services, virtualServices,\n57: // and destinationRules that are accessible to a given\n58: // sidecar. Precomputing the list of services, virtual services, dest rules\n59: // for a sidecar improves performance as we no longer need to compute this\n60: // list for every sidecar. We simply have to match a sidecar to a\n61: // SidecarScope. Note that this is not the same as public/private scoped\n62: // services. The list of services seen by every sidecar scope (namespace\n63: // wide or per workload) depends on the imports, the listeners, and other\n64: // settings.\n65: //\n66: // Every proxy workload of SidecarProxy type will always map to a\n67: // SidecarScope object. We need a\n157: \t// virtualService set per listener and not one per sidecarScope because\n158: \t// each listener imports an independent set of virtual services.\n159: \t// Listener 1 could import a namespace,\n162: \t// with a different path rewrite or no path rewrites.\n163: \tvirtualServices []config.Config\n164: \n165: \tlistenerHosts map[string][]host.Name\n166: }\n167: \n168: const defaultSidecar = \"default-sidecar\"\n169: \n170: // DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace is a sidecar scope object with a default catch all egress listener\n171: // that matches the default Istio behavior: a sidecar has listeners for all services in the mesh\n172: // We use this scope when the user has not set any sidecar Config for a given config namespace.\n173: func DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace(ps *PushContext, configNamespace string) *SidecarScope {\n174: \tdefaultEgressListener := &IstioEgressListenerWrapper{\n175: \t\tIstioListener: &networking.IstioEgressListener{\n176: \t\t\tHosts: []string{\"*/*\"},\n177: \t\t},\n178: \t}\n179: \tdefaultEgressListener.services = ps.servicesExportedToNamespace(configNamespace)\n180: \tdefaultEgressListener.virtualServices = ps.VirtualServicesForGateway(configNamespace, constants.IstioMeshGateway)\n181: \n182: \tout := &SidecarScope{\n183: \t\tName: len(defaultEgressListener.services)),\n189: \t\tconfigDependencies: make(map[uint64]struct{}),\n190: \t\tRootNamespace:      ps.Mesh.RootNamespace,\n191: \t\tVersion:            ps.PushVersion,\n192: \t}\n193: \n194: \t// Now that we have all the services that sidecars using this scope (in\n195: \t// this config namespace) will see, identify all the destinationRules\n196: \t// that these services need\n197: \tfor _, s := range out.services {\n198: \t\t// In some scenarios, there may be multiple Services defined for the same hostname due to ServiceEntry allowing\n199: \t\t// arbitrary hostnames. In these cases, we want to pick the first Service, which is the oldest. This ensures\n200: \t\t// newly created Services cannot take ownership unexpectedly.\n201: \t\t// However, the Service is from Kubernetes it should take precedence over ones not. This prevents someone from\n202: \t\t// \"domain squatting\" on the hostname before a Kubernetes Service is created.\n203: \t\t// This relies on the assumption that\n204: \t\tif existing, f := out.servicesByHostname[s.Hostname]; f &&\n205: \t\t\t!(existing.Attributes.ServiceRegistry != provider.Kubernetes && s.Attributes.ServiceRegistry == provider.Kubernetes) {\n206: \t\t\tcontinue\n207: \t\t}\n208: \t\tout.servicesByHostname[s.Hostname] = s\n209: \t\tif dr := ps.destinationRule(configNamespace, s); dr != nil {\n210: \t\t\tout.destinationRules[s.Hostname] = dr\n211: \t\t}\n212: \t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n213: \t\t\tKind:      gvk.ServiceEntry,\n214: \t\t\tName:      string(s.Hostname),\n215: \t\t\tNamespace: s.Attributes.Namespace,\n216: \t\t})\n217: \t}\n218: \n219: \tfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n220: \t\tfor _, dr := range drList {\n221: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n222: \t\t\t\tKind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n223: \t\t\t\tName:      dr.Name,\n224: \t\t\t\tNamespace: dr.Namespace,\n225: \t\t\t})\n226: \t\t}\n227: \t}\n228: \n229: \tfor _, el := range out.EgressListeners {\n230: \t\t// add dependencies on delegate virtual services\n231: \t\tdelegates := ps.DelegateVirtualServicesConfigKey(el.virtualServices)\n232: \t\tfor _, delegate := range delegates {\n233: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(delegate)\n234: \t\t}\n235: \t\tfor _, vs := range el.virtualServices {\n236: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n237: \t\t\t\tKind:      gvk.VirtualService,\n238: \t\t\t\tName:      vs.Name,\n239: \t\t\t\tNamespace: vs.Namespace,\n240: \t\t\t})\n241: \t\t}\n242: \t}\n243: \n244: \tif ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy != nil {\n245: \t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = &networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy{\n246: \t\t\tMode: networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy_Mode(ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy.Mode),\n247: \t\t}\n248: \t}\n249: \n250: \treturn out\n251: }\n252: \n253: // ConvertToSidecarScope converts from Sidecar config to SidecarScope object\n254: func ConvertToSidecarScope(ps *PushContext, sidecarConfig *config.Config, configNamespace string) *SidecarScope {\n255: \tif sidecarConfig == nil {\n256: \t\treturn DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace(ps, configNamespace)\n257: \t}\n258: \n259: \tsidecar := sidecarConfig.Spec.(*networking.Sidecar)\n260: \tout := &SidecarScope{\n261: \t\tName:               sidecarConfig.Name,\n262: \t\tNamespace:          configNamespace,\n263: \t\tSidecar: \t// this sidecar crd. This is needed to generate CDS output\n288: \tout.services = make([]*Service, 0)\n289: \ttype serviceIndex struct {\n290: \t\tsvc   *Service\n291: \t\tindex int // index record the position of the svc in slice\n292: \t}\n293: \tservicesAdded := make(map[host.Name]serviceIndex)\n294: \taddService := func(s *Service) {\n295: \t\tif s == nil {\n296: \t\t\treturn\n297: \t\t}\n298: \t\tif foundSvc, \t\t\t// we only merge if the found service is in the same namespace as the one we're trying to add\n309: \t\t\tcopied := foundSvc.svc.DeepCopy()\n310: \t\t\tfor _, p := range s.Ports {\n311: priority\n329: \t\tfor _, s := range listener.services {\n330: \t\t\taddService(s)\n331: \t\t}\n332: \t\t// add dependencies on delegate virtual services\n333: \t\tdelegates := listener.services.\n341: \t\t// That way, if there is ambiguity around what hostname to pick, a user can specify the one they\n342: \t\t// want in the hosts field, and the potentially random choice below won't matter\n343: \t\tfor _, vs := range listener.virtualServices {\n344: \t\t\tv := vs.Spec.(*networking.VirtualService)\n345: \t\t\tout.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n346: \t\t\t\tKind: that have already been found eg because they were requested in hosts\n355: \t\t\t\t\tvar vss *Service\n356: \t\t\t\t\tif matchPort {\n357: \t\t\t\t\t\tvss = serviceMatchingListenerPort(s, \t\t\t\t\t// We couldn't find the hostname in our config namespace\n367: \t\t\t\t\t// We have to pick one arbitrarily for now, so we'll pick the first namespace alphabetically\n368: \t\t\t\t\t// TODO: could we choose services more intelligently based on their ports?\n369: \t\t\t\t\tbyNamespace := ps.ServiceIndex.HostnameAndNamespace[host.Name(h)]\n370: \t\t\t\t\tif len(byNamespace) == 0 {\n371: \t\t\t\t\t\t// This hostname isn't found anywhere\n372: \t\t\t\t\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Could not find service hostname %s parsed from %s\", h, vs.Key())\n373: \t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n374: \t\t\t\t\t}\n375: alphabetically\n385: \t\t\t\t\t\t// This won't overwrite hostnames that have already been found eg because they were requested in hosts\n386: \t\t\t\t\t\tvar vss *Service\n387: \t\t\t\t\t\tif \t\t\t\t\t\tif vss != nil {\n393: \t\t\t\t\t\t\taddService(vss)\n394: \t\t\t\t\t\t}\n395: \t\t\t\t\t}\n396: \t\t\t\t}\n397: \t\t\t}\n398: \t\t}\n399: \t}\n400: \n401: \t// Now that we have all the services that sidecars using this scope (in\n402: \t// this config namespace) will see, identify all the destinationRules\n403: \t// that these services need\n404: \tout.servicesByHostname = \t\t\t\t})\n416: \t\t\t}\n417: \t\t}\n418: \t}\n419: \n420: \tif sidecar.OutboundTrafficPolicy == nil {\n421: \t\tif ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy != nil {\n422: \t\t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = &networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy{\n423: \t\t\t\tMode: networking.OutboundTrafficPolicy_Mode(ps.Mesh.OutboundTrafficPolicy.Mode),\n424: \t\t\t}\n425: \t\t}\n426: \t} else {\n427: \t\tout.OutboundTrafficPolicy = sidecar.OutboundTrafficPolicy\n428: \t}\n429: \n430: \treturn out\n431: }\n432: \n433: func convertIstioListenerToWrapper(ps *PushContext, configNamespace string,\n434: \tistioListener *networking.IstioEgressListener) *IstioEgressListenerWrapper {\n435: \tout := &IstioEgressListenerWrapper{\n436: \t\tIstioListener: istioListener,\n437: \t}\n438: \n439: listener port or the bind address or the catch all listener\n465: func (sc *SidecarScope) GetEgressListenerForRDS(port int, bind string) *IstioEgressListenerWrapper {\n466: \tif sc == nil {\n467: \t\treturn nil\n468: \t}\n469: \n470: \tfor _, e := range sc.EgressListeners {\n471: \t\t// We hit a catchall listener. == 0 { // unix domain socket\n481: \t\t\t\tif e.IstioListener.Bind == bind {\n482: \t\t\t\t\treturn e\n483: \t\t\t\t}\n484: \t\t\t\t// no match.. continue searching\n485: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n486: \t\t\t}\n487: \t\t\t// this is a non-zero port match\n488: \t\t\treturn e\n489: \t\t}\n490: \t}\n491: \n492: \t// This should never be reached unless user explicitly set an empty array for egress\n493: \t// listeners which we actually forbid\n494: \treturn nil\n495: }\n496: \n497: // HasIngressListener returns if the sidecar scope has ingress listener set\n498: func (sc *SidecarScope) AddConfigDependencies add extra config dependencies to this scope. This action should be done before the\n543: // SidecarScope being used to avoid concurrent read/write.\n544: func (sc *SidecarScope) AddConfigDependencies(dependencies ...ConfigKey) {\n545: \tif sc == {\n553: \t\tsc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()] = struct{}{}\n554: \t}\n555: }\n556: \n557: // DestinationRule returns a destinationrule for a svc.\n558: func (sc *SidecarScope) DestinationRule(direction TrafficDirection, proxy *Proxy, svc host.Name) *config.Config {\n559: \tdestinationRules := sc.destinationRules[svc]\n560: \tvar catchAllDr *config.Config\n561: \tfor _, destRule := range destinationRules {\n562: \t\tdestinationRule := destRule.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n563: \t\tif destinationRule.GetWorkloadSelector() == nil {\n564: \t\t\tcatchAllDr = destRule\n565: \t\t}\n566: \t\t// filter DestinationRule based on workloadSelector for outbound configs.\n567: \t\t// WorkloadSelector configuration is honored only for outbound configuration, because\n568: \t\t// for inbound configuration, the settings at sidecar would be more explicit and the preferred way forward.\n569: \t\tif sc.Namespace == destRule.Namespace &&\n570: labels.Instance(destinationRule.GetWorkloadSelector().GetMatchLabels())\n573: \t\t\t// return destination rule if workload selector matches\n574: \t\t\tif workloadLabels.IsSupersetOf(workloadSelector) {\n575: \t\t\t\treturn destRule\n576: \t\t\t}\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: \t// If there is no workload specific destinationRule, return the wild carded dr if present.\n580: \tif catchAllDr != nil []*Service {\n588: \treturn sc.services\n589: }\n590: \n591: // Return filtered services through the hosts field in the egress portion of the Sidecar config.\n592: // Note that the returned service could be trimmed.\n593: func (ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) selectServices(services []*Service, configNamespace string, hosts map[string][]host.Name) []*Service {\n594: \timportedServices := make([]*Service, 0)\n595: \twildcardHosts, wnsFound := hosts[wildcardNamespace]\n596: \tfor _, s := range services {\n597: \t\tconfigNamespace := s.Attributes.Namespace\n598: \n599: \t\t// Check if there is an explicit import of form ns/* or ns/host\n600: \t\tif importedHosts, nsFound := hosts[configNamespace]; nsFound {\n601: \t\t\tif svc := matchingService(importedHosts, s, ilw); svc != nil {\n602: \t\t\t\timportedServices = append(importedServices, svc)\n603: \t\t\t}\n604: \t\t} else if wnsFound { // Check if there is an import of form */host or */*\n605: \t\t\tif svc := matchingService(wildcardHosts, s, ilw); svc != nil {\n606: \t\t\t\timportedServices = append(importedServices, svc)\n607: \t\t\t}\n608: \t\t}\n609: \t}\n610: \n611: \tvalidServices := make(map[host.Name]string)\n612: \tfor _, svc := range importedServices {\n613: \t\t_, f := validServices[svc.Hostname]\n614: \t\t// Select a single namespace for a given hostname.\n615: \t\t// If the same hostname is imported from multiple namespaces, pick the one in the configNamespace\n616: \t\t// If neither are in configNamespace, an arbitrary one will be chosen\n617: \t\tif !f || svc.Attributes.Namespace == configNamespace {\n618: \t\t\tvalidServices[svc.Hostname] = svc.Attributes.Namespace\n619: \t\t}\n620: \t}\n621: \n622: \tfilteredServices := make([]*Service, 0)\n623: \t// Filter down to just instances in scope for the service\n624: \tfor _, svc := range importedServices {\n625: \t\tif validServices[svc.Hostname] == svc.Attributes.Namespace {\n626: \t\t\tfilteredServices = append(filteredServices, svc)\n627: \t\t}\n628: \t}\n629: \treturn filteredServices\n630: }\n631: \n632: // Return the original service or a trimmed service which has a subset of the ports in original service.\n633: func matchingService(importedHosts []host.Name, service *Service, ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) *Service {\n634: \tmatchPort := needsPortMatch(ilw)\n635: \tfor _, importedHost := range importedHosts {\n636: \t\t// Check if the hostnames match per usual hostname matching rules\n637: \t\tif service.Hostname.SubsetOf(importedHost) {\n638: \t\t\tif serviceMatchingListenerPort constructs service with listener port.\n648: func serviceMatchingListenerPort(service *Service, ilw *IstioEgressListenerWrapper) *Service {\n649: \tfor _, port := range {
  "content": "# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update\n\n## Summary\n\nWhen multiple DestinationRules target the same host, updating one of them fails to trigger an xDS push to Envoy sidecars because only one DR's metadata is retained during merging, causing the other DR's ConfigKey to never be registered in the proxy's config dependencies, leading to change detection failure.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause spans three interconnected systems:\n\n1. **DestinationRule Merging Loss of Identity** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`)\n2. **Incomplete Config Dependency Registration** (`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227, 410-416`)\n3. **xDS Push Filter Using Missing Dependencies** (`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:52-74`)\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. DestinationRule Merging Loses Metadata Identity\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`\n\nThe `mergeDestinationRule()` function merges multiple DRs for the same FQDN host into a single consolidated rule:\n\n```go\nfunc (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig config.Config, exportToMap map[visibility.Instance]bool) {\n    rule := destRuleConfig.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n    resolvedHost := ResolveShortnameToFQDN(rule.Host, destRuleConfig.Meta)\n\n    if mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {\n        // ... matching logic ...\n        for i, mdr := range mdrList {\n            // Line 65-66: Deep copy and update existing rule in place\n            copied := mdr.DeepCopy()\n            p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied\n            mergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)\n\n            // Lines 77-87: Merge subsets from new rule into existing rule\n            for _, subset := range rule.Subsets {\n                // append subsets to existing rule\n                mergedRule.Subsets = append(mergedRule.Subsets, subset)\n            }\n\n            // Lines 91-93: Merge traffic policy if not present\n            if mergedRule.TrafficPolicy == nil && rule.TrafficPolicy != nil {\n                mergedRule.TrafficPolicy = rule.TrafficPolicy\n            }\n        }\n        if addRuleToProcessedDestRules {\n            // New rule is added to list\n            p.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n        }\n        return\n    }\n\n    // First rule is simply added\n    p.destRules[resolvedHost] = append(p.destRules[resolvedHost], &destRuleConfig)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue:** When two DRs are merged:\n- The first DR's config metadata (Name=\"reviews-traffic-policy\", Namespace=\"default\") is preserved\n- The second DR's metadata (Name=\"reviews-subsets\", Namespace=\"default\") is lost\u2014only its Spec (subsets, traffic policy) is merged into the first DR's config\n- `p.destRules[resolvedHost]` contains only ONE config.Config element after merging, with the first DR's metadata\n\n### 2. Config Dependency Registration Only Tracks Surviving DR\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227` (in `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()`)\n\n```go\n// Lines 219-227\nfor _, drList := range out.destinationRules {\n    for _, dr := range drList {\n        out.AddConfigDependencies(ConfigKey{\n            Kind:      gvk.DestinationRule,\n            Name:      dr.Name,                    // Only the FIRST DR's name survives here\n            Namespace: dr.Namespace,\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue:**\n- `out.destinationRules` is populated from `ps.destinationRule(configNamespace, s)` (line 209)\n- This method returns the merged destination rules from `consolidatedDestRules`\n- Since only one DR's metadata survives the merge, only ONE ConfigKey is registered\n- When a new SidecarScope is created (line 254, `ConvertToSidecarScope()`), the same issue occurs at lines 410-416\n\n### 3. config.Config Metadata Structure\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go:251-256`\n\n```go\ntype consolidatedDestRules struct {\n    // Map of dest rule host to the list of namespaces to which this destination rule has been exported to\n    exportTo map[host.Name]map[visibility.Instance]bool\n    // Map of dest rule host and the merged destination rules for that host\n    destRules map[host.Name][]*config.Config  // Only ONE config.Config survives per host!\n}\n```\n\n### 4. xDS Push Filter Uses Missing Dependencies\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:52-74`\n\n```go\nfunc ConfigAffectsProxy(req *model.PushRequest, proxy *model.Proxy) bool {\n    for config := range req.ConfigsUpdated {\n        // ... type checking ...\n        if affected && checkProxyDependencies(proxy, config) {\n            return true\n        }\n    }\n    return false\n}\n\nfunc checkProxyDependencies(proxy *model.Proxy, config model.ConfigKey) bool {\n    switch proxy.Type {\n    case model.SidecarProxy:\n        // LINE 64: Calls DependsOnConfig with the updated DR's ConfigKey\n        if proxy.SidecarScope.DependsOnConfig(config) {\n            return true\n        }\n        // ...\n    }\n    return false\n}\n```\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:523-540` (in `DependsOnConfig()`)\n\n```go\nfunc (sc *SidecarScope) DependsOnConfig(config ConfigKey) bool {\n    if sc == nil {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    if _, f := clusterScopedConfigTypes[config.Kind]; f {\n        return config.Namespace == sc.RootNamespace || config.Namespace == sc.Namespace\n    }\n\n    if _, f := sidecarScopeKnownConfigTypes[config.Kind]; !f {\n        return true\n    }\n\n    // LINE 538: Check if the ConfigKey's hash is in the registered dependencies\n    _, exists := sc.configDependencies[config.HashCode()]\n    return exists\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue:** When a DestinationRule update event occurs:\n1. The event contains the ConfigKey for the updated DR: `{Kind: DestinationRule, Name: \"reviews-subsets\", Namespace: \"default\"}`\n2. This ConfigKey's hash is computed (lines 60-74 in `pilot/pkg/model/config.go`)\n3. `DependsOnConfig()` checks if this hash exists in `configDependencies`\n4. Since only \"reviews-traffic-policy\" was registered, the hash for \"reviews-subsets\" is NOT in the map\n5. `DependsOnConfig()` returns `false`\n6. The xDS push is SKIPPED\n\n### 5. Hash Computation\n\n**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/config.go:60-74`\n\n```go\nfunc (key ConfigKey) HashCode() uint64 {\n    hash := md5.New()\n    for _, v := range []string{\n        key.Name,\n        key.Namespace,\n        key.Kind.Kind,\n        key.Kind.Group,\n        key.Kind.Version,\n    } {\n        hash.Write([]byte(v))\n    }\n    var tmp [md5.Size]byte\n    sum := hash.Sum(tmp[:0])\n    return binary.BigEndian.Uint64(sum)\n}\n```\n\nThe hash includes the DR's Name, so:\n- \"reviews-traffic-policy\" \u2192 hash H1 (registered)\n- \"reviews-subsets\" \u2192 hash H2 (NOT registered)\n\nWhen \"reviews-subsets\" is updated, its ConfigKey generates hash H2, which is not in `configDependencies`, so the push is rejected.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go`**\n   - `mergeDestinationRule()` - loses DR identity during merge\n\n2. **`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go`**\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` - only registers one DR's ConfigKey\n   - `ConvertToSidecarScope()` - only registers one DR's ConfigKey\n   - `AddConfigDependencies()` - called with incomplete list of DRs\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` - correctly checks dependencies but only has one DR's key\n\n3. **`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go`**\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` - correctly filters based on dependencies\n   - `checkProxyDependencies()` - correctly checks if proxy depends on config\n\n4. **`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`**\n   - `destinationRule()` - returns merged DRs with only one metadata\n   - `consolidatedDestRules` - stores only one config.Config per host\n   - `destinationRuleIndex` - stores consolidated rules without tracking all contributors\n\n5. **`pilot/pkg/model/config.go`**\n   - `ConfigKey.HashCode()` - correctly hashes individual keys, but only some keys are registered\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Operator updates `reviews-subsets` DR \u2192 Envoy sidecar receives no xDS update\n2. **Event Propagation**: Istio control plane detects the DestinationRule update event\n3. **Push Filtering (FAILURE POINT)**: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` is called with ConfigKey{Name: \"reviews-subsets\", ...}\n4. **Dependency Check**: `DependsOnConfig()` is called, which checks if hash of \"reviews-subsets\" is in `configDependencies`\n5. **Missing Dependency**: The hash for \"reviews-subsets\" is NOT found (only \"reviews-traffic-policy\" was registered)\n6. **Push Rejected**: `ConfigAffectsProxy()` returns `false`, push is skipped\n7. **Root Cause - Incomplete Registration**: Only \"reviews-traffic-policy\"'s ConfigKey was added to dependencies because:\n   - `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` or `ConvertToSidecarScope()` called `ps.destinationRule()` which returned the merged DR\n   - The merged DR list contained only ONE config.Config (with \"reviews-traffic-policy\" metadata)\n   - Only one ConfigKey was registered via `AddConfigDependencies()`\n8. **Root Cause - Merging**: Only one DR's metadata survived the merge because:\n   - When `mergeDestinationRule()` processed the second DR, it merged its Spec into the first DR's config\n   - It never added a second config.Config to the `destRules[host]` list (unless workload selectors required it)\n   - The second DR's metadata was discarded\n\n## Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo verify this root cause in a live cluster:\n\n1. **Inspect the merged DR list:**\n   ```bash\n   kubectl port-forward -n istio-system <istiod-pod> 8080:8080\n   curl http://localhost:8080/debug/configz | jq '.destinationRules'\n   ```\n   Check that only ONE DR's Name/Namespace appears per host, despite multiple DRs being defined.\n\n2. **Inspect the SidecarScope dependencies:**\n   ```bash\n   curl http://localhost:8080/debug/configz | jq '.sidecarScopes[].configDependencies'\n   ```\n   Verify that only one DestinationRule ConfigKey is registered.\n\n3. **Trace the update event:**\n   Enable debug logging in Istiod and watch for:\n   - The DestinationRule update event being received\n   - `ConfigAffectsProxy()` being called with the updated DR's ConfigKey\n   - `DependsOnConfig()` returning `false` (no push triggered)\n\n4. **Compare with a single DR:**\n   Define only one DestinationRule per host and verify that updates DO trigger xDS pushes.\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Fix Strategy:**\n\nThe solution requires registering ALL contributing DestinationRules in the SidecarScope dependencies, not just the one whose metadata survives the merge.\n\n### Option 1: Track Contributing DRs During Merge (Preferred)\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules` to maintain a list of contributing DR ConfigKeys alongside the merged config\n- When creating SidecarScope dependencies, iterate over ALL contributing DRs, not just the merged result\n- **Impact**: Preserves the current merging behavior while fixing dependency tracking\n\n### Option 2: Store All DRs Without Merging Metadata\n- Modify `consolidatedDestRules.destRules` to keep multiple config.Config entries (one per source DR)\n- Only merge the Spec (subsets, traffic policy) into the first DR's config\n- Preserve each original DR's metadata separately\n- **Impact**: Requires changes to how merged DRs are retrieved by consumers\n\n### Option 3: Separate Merging from Dependency Tracking\n- Create a mapping from merged DR ConfigKey to all contributing DR ConfigKeys\n- When checking dependencies, include both direct matches and merged-into matches\n- **Impact**: Requires cross-referencing in the dependency lookup path\n\n**Minimal Necessary Fix:**\n1. In `consolidatedDestRules`, add a field: `contributingDRs map[host.Name][]ConfigKey` to track all contributing DR identities\n2. In `mergeDestinationRule()`, append each source DR's ConfigKey to the contributing list\n3. In `DefaultSidecarScopeForNamespace()` and `ConvertToSidecarScope()`, iterate over contributing DRs instead of just the merged result\n4. Update `DependsOnConfig()` or the push filter to recognize that a proxy depends on a DR if it depends on any merged variant of that DR\n\nThis ensures that when ANY contributing DR is updated, the proxy receives the push.\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report: Stale Envoy Route Configuration After DestinationRule Update

## Summary

When multiple DestinationRules target the same host, updating one of them fails to trigger an xDS push to Envoy sidecars because only one DR's metadata is retained during merging, causing the other DR's ConfigKey to never be registered in the proxy's config dependencies, leading to change detection failure.

## Root Cause

The root cause spans three interconnected systems:

1. **DestinationRule Merging Loss of Identity** (`pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`)
2. **Incomplete Config Dependency Registration** (`pilot/pkg/model/sidecar.go:219-227, 410-416`)
3. **xDS Push Filter Using Missing Dependencies** (`pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go:52-74`)

## Evidence

### 1. DestinationRule Merging Loses Metadata Identity

**File:** `pilot/pkg/model/destination_rule.go:38-109`

The `mergeDestinationRule()` function merges multiple DRs for the same FQDN host into a single consolidated rule:

```go
func (ps *PushContext) mergeDestinationRule(p *consolidatedDestRules, destRuleConfig config.Config, exportToMap map[visibility.Instance]bool) {
    rule := destRuleConfig.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)
    resolvedHost := ResolveShortnameToFQDN(rule.Host, destRuleConfig.Meta)

    if mdrList, exists := p.destRules[resolvedHost]; exists {
        // ... matching logic ...
        for i, mdr := range mdrList {
            // Line 65-66: Deep copy and update existing rule in place
            copied := mdr.DeepCopy()
            p.destRules[resolvedHost][i] = &copied
            mergedRule := copied.Spec.(*networking.DestinationRule)

            // Lines 77-87: Merge subsets from new rule into existing rule
            for _, subset := range rule.Subsets {
                // ap
... (truncated)
